## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma as stress, epsilon as strain, and T as temperature, the task most naturally fits thermomechanical constitutive laws used in materials science to model elastic/plastic stress–strain behavior with temperature-dependent stiffness, yield/flow stress, and thermal strain effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential): sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (rapid softening/stiffening with T)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain subtraction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (constraint-induced stress from mismatch/thermal expansion)
- Polynomial nonlinear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate nonlinear elastic response)
- Piecewise-like smooth tension/compression asymmetry: sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)) * epsilon (different slope in tension vs compression, smooth via Abs)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow curve / strain hardening)
- Ludwik-type offset power-law: sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (yield offset plus hardening; avoids singular at epsilon=0)
- Ramberg–Osgood-inspired (inverted power form): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (empirical nonlinear stress–strain mapping)
- Thermal softening of flow stress (multiplicative): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (hardening with epsilon, softening/stiffening with T via exponent sign)
- Johnson–Cook-like strain hardening with thermal softening (no rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T)**c5 (captures decreasing strength with increasing T up to a cutoff)
- Entropic (rubber-like) thermoelasticity using stretch lambda=1+epsilon: sigma = c0 * T * ((1 + epsilon) - (1 + epsilon)**(-2)) (polymer network elasticity; strong T coupling)
- Hyperelastic rational form (finite-strain-type curvature): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1) / (c2 + epsilon) (nonlinear stiffening/softening while remaining bounded away from singularities via shifts)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon, with the proportionality (effective modulus) varying smoothly with T (e.g., c0 + c1*T or c0*exp(c1*T)).
- Thermal strain under constraint → sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T-T0)); look for linear combination of epsilon and T with a subtractive structure inside parentheses.
- Plastic hardening curves → monotone concave/convex relationships often fit by power laws in epsilon (epsilon**n) or shifted power laws (epsilon + c)**n to handle initial yield offsets.
- Thermal softening of strength → multiplicative separation is common: (hardening in epsilon) * (softening in T); the T-factor often decreases with T via a negative exponent or via (c0 - c1*T)**m with a cutoff.
- Tension–compression asymmetry or sign effects → structures involving Abs(epsilon) multiplied by epsilon can change tangent stiffness with strain magnitude while preserving stress sign.
- Finite-strain kinematics (especially polymers/elastomers) → stress often depends on stretch (1+epsilon) and may include terms like (1+epsilon)**p and (1+epsilon)**(-q), producing strong nonlinearity as epsilon approaches -1.
- Near-transition behavior (e.g., approaching softening at high T) → expect rapid curvature in T-dependence; exponentials or high-order polynomials in T can emulate sharp drops without explicit phase variables.
- Empirical bounded response (avoiding unphysical divergence) → rational forms with shifted epsilon (epsilon+c)/(c+epsilon) or (epsilon+c)/(c+epsilon+c) can mimic saturation-like stiffening/softening while staying finite.

Rewrite to expose structure:
\[
=6.531365700567425\,\epsilon^3\;+\;(-0.6867651335523405+3.018423785145038\log(\epsilon+1))\,T\;+\;\text{(constant in }T\text{ depending on }\epsilon).
\]
Key properties:
- Has an \(\epsilon^3\) term independent of \(T\).
- Has a \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\) term.
- Has a linear-in-\(T\) term with coefficient \(-0.6867...\) (independent of \(\epsilon\)).
- Uses \(\log(\epsilon+1)\) (not \(\log(\epsilon^2+1)\), not \(\log(|\epsilon|+1)\) unless we impose \(\epsilon\ge 0\) and also match the shift \(+1\) exactly).

Now check candidates.

1) Contains \(c7 e^{Tc8}\log(c9|\epsilon|+1)\) (exponential in \(T\)), and polynomial/rational in \(\epsilon\). GT is linear in \(T\), not \(e^{kT}\). Setting \(c8=0\) makes that term \(c7\log(c9|\epsilon|+1)\) (no \(T\log\) term). No way to create \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\). Not match.

2) Entire expression is sums of terms all divided by \((\epsilon+1)\). GT has no global \((\epsilon+1)^{-1}\) factor. You could try to cancel by choosing coefficients so numerator equals GT\(\cdot(\epsilon+1)\), but the available basis terms are limited (mostly linear/quadratic in \(\epsilon\) times \(T\) and \(\log\) all over \(\epsilon+1\)). GT has \(\epsilon^3\) (no denominator). Cannot match for a continuous domain. Not match.
